tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:238px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CornwallConstituencies2010.gif" class="image"><img alt="" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CornwallConstituencies2010.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sketchmap of 2010 parliamentary constituencies in Cornwall - click to enlarge</div></div></div>\n<p><b>St Ives</b> is a parliamentary <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_Kingdom_Parliament_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of United Kingdom Parliament constituencies">constituency</a> in west Cornwall; it includes the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup>. The constituency has been represented in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">UK Parliament</a> since 2015 by <a href="/wiki/Derek_Thomas_(politician)" title="Derek Thomas (politician)">Derek Thomas</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative</a> MP.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;n 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32"><a href="#Sources"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>St Ives has elected MPs to every Parliament since 1558, except for a brief period during the <a href="/wiki/English_Protectorate" class="mw-redirect" title="English Protectorate">Protectorate</a>. It was originally a mere <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_borough" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary borough">parliamentary borough</a> that returned two MPs until the <a href="/wiki/Great_Reform_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Reform Act">Great Reform Act</a> of 1832, when its representation was cut to a single member. In 1885 the borough was abolished, but the St Ives name was transferred to the surrounding <a href="/wiki/County_constituency" class="mw-redirect" title="County constituency">county constituency</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St_Ives_borough">St Ives borough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: St Ives borough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The borough established under <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">Queen Mary</a> consisted of the parish of <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cornwall" title="St Ives, Cornwall">St Ives</a> in western <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, a seaport and market town in which the main economic interests were fishing and the export of ores mined nearby. In 1831, the population of the borough was 4,776, and contained 1,002 houses.\n</p><p>The franchise was initially restricted to the town corporation, but after a judgment in a disputed election in 1702 the right to vote was given to all inhabitants paying <a href="/wiki/Scot_and_lot" title="Scot and lot">scot and lot</a>; in the early 19th century this amounted to a little over 300 voters. This was a wide franchise for the period, and its reasonable size meant that St Ives was one of the few Cornish boroughs that could claim not to be <a href="/wiki/Cornish_rotten_boroughs" class="mw-redirect" title="Cornish rotten boroughs">rotten</a>.\n</p><p>Elections were usually contested and although local wealthiest families were able to exercise considerable influence on the outcome, none was entirely predominant; the result could rarely be taken for granted and it was necessary to court the voters assiduously. From the 17th century, three vied for control - the <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Buckinghamshire" title="Earl of Buckinghamshire">Hobart family</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;n 3&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Praed_Street" title="Praed Street">Praeds</a> (at the time of Treventhoe manor), and the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Bolton" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Bolton">Dukes of Bolton</a><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;n 4&#93;</a></sup> - and by the mid 18th century the Stephens family had considerable sway. In 1751, however, John Stephens, who had previously allied himself with the Earl of Buckinghamshire and managed the borough\'s elections on the Earl\'s behalf, "struck out on his own account" (for his own interests) and secured the election of his son. Later in the decade Stephens and the Earl once more began to work together, but were unable to prevent Humphrey Mackworth Praed from establishing sufficient influence to sway one of the two seats.\n</p><p>But by 1761 the alliances had shifted again, Buckinghamshire and Praed on one side nominating candidates against Stephens and the Duke of Bolton on the other. The by-election in 1763, when Buckinghamshire\'s brother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Sir_Charles_Hotham-Thompson,_8th_Baronet" title="Sir Charles Hotham-Thompson, 8th Baronet">Charles Hotham</a> was re-elected after being appointed to a position in the Royal Household, cost the Earl \xc2\xa31,175 even though his candidate was eventually returned unopposed - the expenditure included payments of 7 guineas to each of 124 people.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;n 5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There was a further bitterly contested election in 1774: allegations of bribery were investigated by a House of Commons committee, whose proceedings are recounted at length by the contemporary historian of electoral abuses, Thomas Oldfield.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;n 6&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Stephens_(senior)" title="Samuel Stephens (senior)">Samuel Stephens</a>, defeated by 7 votes, accused <a href="/wiki/William_Praed" title="William Praed">William Praed</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adam_Drummond" title="Adam Drummond">Adam Drummond</a> (the Duke of Bolton\'s candidate) of benefiting from several types of corruption. Humphrey Mackworth Praed, William\'s father, was said to have lent large sums to voters on the understanding that repayment would not be demanded if they voted for Praed and Drummond; but <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/counsel" class="extiw" title="wikt:counsel">counsel</a> for Praed and Drummond adduced evidence that Stephens had also resorted to bribery. However, it was alleged that many of Stephens\' supporters had been prevented from voting, by rating them as not liable for scot and lot and so not eligible to vote; this was a frequent abuse in such boroughs.  His side, as petitioners, failed to bring any evidence of criminal misconduct by the parish overseers so the committee decided they had no jurisdiction to interfere. In the end, the committee upheld Drummond\'s election but declared that neither Stephens nor Praed had been properly elected, and a writ was issued for a by-election to fill the second seat.\n</p><p>The cost of electioneering in St Ives seems eventually to have led to Buckinghamshire and Bolton withdrawing, and by 1784 Praed was considered unchallenged as patron. Nevertheless, Stephens\' influence was not extinguished, and it was recorded that the patrons at the time of the <a href="/wiki/Reform_Act" title="Reform Act">Reform Act</a> were <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Stephens_(junior)" title="Samuel Stephens (junior)">Samuel Stephens</a> of Tregarron and <a href="/wiki/Sir_Christopher_Hawkins,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir Christopher Hawkins, 1st Baronet">Sir Christopher Hawkins</a> of Trewithan (who had purchased the manor of Mr Praed).\n</p><p>The Reform Act extended the boundaries of the constituency, bringing in the neighbouring parishes of <a href="/wiki/Lelant" title="Lelant">Lelant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Towednack" title="Towednack">Towednack</a>; nevertheless, the borough lost one of its two seats. There were 584 qualified voters at the first reformed election, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1832" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom general election, 1832">that of 1832</a>.\n</p><p>Even with a further extension of the franchise in 1868, the electorate never passed 1,500, and had fallen to barely 1,000 by <a href="/wiki/Redistribution_of_Seats_Act_1885" title="Redistribution of Seats Act 1885">the next Reform Act</a>, under which the borough was abolished <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1885" title="United Kingdom general election, 1885">that year</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="St_Ives_county_constituency">St Ives county constituency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: St Ives county constituency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dt>1885-1918</dt></dl>\n<p>Division of counties into single-member constituencies was effected in 1885: Cornwall having six. The westernmost of these, in which St Ives stood, was formally <b>The Western or St Ives Division of Cornwall</b> but was most often referred to simply as <b>St Ives</b> or as <b>West Cornwall</b>.\n</p><p>This area included <a href="/wiki/Penzance" title="Penzance">Penzance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul,_Cornwall" title="Paul, Cornwall">Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ludgvan" title="Ludgvan">Ludgvan</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Just_in_Penwith" title="St Just in Penwith">St Just</a>, and stretched not only from <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End" title="Land&#39;s End">Land\'s End</a> to <a href="/wiki/St_Erth" title="St Erth">St Erth</a> but also included the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>. This <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Cornwall" title="Duchy of Cornwall">duchy seat</a> was abnormally low in owner-occupiers, with many "<a href="/wiki/Nonconformism" class="mw-redirect" title="Nonconformism">nonconformist</a>" Christians<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservatives</a> were consequently very weak. However, local sentiment was strongly against <a href="/wiki/Irish_Home_Rule" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Home Rule">Irish Home Rule</a> or independence, seen as a particular threat to the livelihood of the fishermen and other maritime employees who made up much of the electorate, and St Ives therefore became a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Unionist" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal Unionist">Liberal Unionist</a> stronghold from 1886.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;n 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<dl><dt>1918-1983</dt></dl>\n<p>After the boundary revisions introduced at the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1918" title="United Kingdom general election, 1918">general election of 1918</a>, which brought in most of the villages on the <a href="/wiki/Lizard_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Lizard Peninsula">Lizard Peninsula</a> (though not <a href="/wiki/Helston" title="Helston">Helston</a>), the constituency was simply called <b>Cornwall, St Ives</b>. It underwent further boundary changes in 1950, bringing <a href="/wiki/Helston" title="Helston">Helston</a> into the constituency, and in 1983, when it was extended to include all of the <a href="/wiki/Penwith" title="Penwith">Penwith</a> local government district.\n</p><p>The character of the constituency was little changed any of these revisions, but party loyalties may have been disrupted by the 1918 changes. <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> put up a candidate for the first time in 1918, and took more than a third of the vote; at the next election, with Labour withdrawing and the Irish issue no longer able to help Cory, a Conservative was elected for the first time. For the next decade St Ives was a Conservative-Liberal marginal, changing hands four times in the 1920s. However, the formal split of <a href="/wiki/National_Liberal_Party_(UK,_1931)" title="National Liberal Party (UK, 1931)">National Liberals</a> from the Liberals offered a popular compromise which suited the voters, so much so as to be a <a href="/wiki/Safe_seat" title="Safe seat">safe seat</a>, and later for Conservatives when the National Liberals finally merged with them in the 1960s, until the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrats</a> re-invigorated the competition in the 1990s.  <a href="/wiki/Andrew_George_(politician)" title="Andrew George (politician)">Andrew George</a> captured the seat after the retirement of the sitting Conservative MP in <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1997" title="United Kingdom general election, 1997">1997</a>, and took <a href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute majority">over half the vote</a> in both <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2001" title="United Kingdom general election, 2001">2001</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2005" title="United Kingdom general election, 2005">2005</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prominent_members">Prominent members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Prominent members">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<dl><dt>1885-date</dt></dl>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Walter_Runciman,_1st_Viscount_Runciman_of_Doxford" title="Walter Runciman, 1st Viscount Runciman of Doxford">Walter Runciman</a> held the most senior positions in Education, Agriculture and Trade taking together the period from 1908 until 1916 during the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Government_1905-1915" class="mw-redirect" title="Liberal Government 1905-1915">Asquith ministry</a>.  He was later re-appointed as the most senior minister in Trade from 1931 to 1937 in the all-party <a href="/wiki/UK_National_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="UK National Government">National Coalition Government</a>.\n</p><p>Sir <a href="/wiki/John_Nott" title="John Nott">John Nott</a> also held the most senior position in the Trade department before becoming <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Defence" title="Secretary of State for Defence">Secretary of State for Defence</a>, including during the <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentine</a> invasion of the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> and the ensuing <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>.  His assertion that he was cutting the defence budget before the war was not capricious and he offered his resignation to <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, however she kept him for the duration of the conflict and he stood down in 1983.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Usual_late_count_in_modern_elections">Usual late count in modern elections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Usual late count in modern elections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>At general elections, the constituency is usually one of the last to declare a result - the delay in bringing the ballot boxes over from the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a> means that counting does not begin until the following day.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In the 2015 general election it was the last constituency in the United Kingdom to declare, because the ballot boxes were flown in from the Isles of Scilly only on the first scheduled flight the following morning, having been kept in police cells overnight on <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s,_Isles_of_Scilly" title="St Mary&#39;s, Isles of Scilly">St Mary\'s</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> with the declaration taking place at 15:30 on Friday afternoon.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> However, in 1987 and 1992 the constituency did count during the night rather than the next day. The seat was declared at about 1:30 am in 1987 and about 3:45 am in 1992.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Boundaries">Boundaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Boundaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p><b>1885-1918</b>: The Municipal Boroughs of Penzance and St Ives, the Sessional Division of West Penwith (including the Isles of Scilly), and the civil parishes of St Erth and Uny-Lelant.\n</p><p><b>1918-1950</b>: The Municipal Boroughs of Penzance and St Ives, the Urban Districts of Ludgvan, Madron, Paul, and St Just, the Rural District of West Penwith, the Isles of Scilly, and part of the Rural District of Helston.\n</p><p><b>1950-1983</b>: The Municipal Boroughs of Helston, Penzance, and St Ives, the Urban District of St Just, the Isles of Scilly, and parts of the Rural Districts of Kerrier and West Penwith.\n</p><p><b>1983-2010</b>: The District of Penwith, the District of Kerrier wards of Breage and Germoe, Crowan, Grade-Ruan and Landewednack, Helston North, Helston South, Meneage, Mullion, Porthleven, St Keverne and Wendron, and Sithney, and the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p><b>2010-present</b>: The District of Penwith wards of Goldsithney, Gulval and Heamoor, Lelant and Carbis Bay, Ludgvan and Towednack, Madron and Zennor, Marazion and Perranuthnoe, Morvah, Pendeen and St Just, Penzance Central, Penzance East, Penzance Promenade, Penzance South, St Buryan, St Erth and St Hilary, St Ives North, and St Ives South, the District of Kerrier wards of Breage and Crowan, Grade-Ruan and Landewednack, Helston North, Helston South, Meneage, Mullion, Porthleven and Sithney, and St Keverne, and the Isles of Scilly.\n</p><p>The St Ives constituency covers the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>, taking in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_extreme_points_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of extreme points of the United Kingdom">most southerly and westerly points</a> of England (both its mainland and if islands are included), taking in parts of the former <a href="/wiki/Penwith" title="Penwith">Penwith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kerrier" title="Kerrier">Kerrier</a> Districts. The main towns in the constituency are <a href="/wiki/Penzance" title="Penzance">Penzance</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Ives,_Cornwall" title="St Ives, Cornwall">St Ives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Helston" title="Helston">Helston</a>. It also includes the <a href="/wiki/Isles_of_Scilly" title="Isles of Scilly">Isles of Scilly</a>, not shown on the map (having 1,700 electors out of a total of 63,000). The seat includes the <a href="/wiki/Tate_St_Ives" title="Tate St Ives">Tate St Ives</a>, <a href="/wiki/St_Michael%27s_Mount" title="St Michael&#39;s Mount">St Michael\'s Mount</a> (also an island) and <a href="/wiki/Land%27s_End" title="Land&#39;s End">Land\'s End</a>.\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Boundary_Commission_for_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Boundary Commission for England">Boundary Commission</a>\' <a href="/wiki/Fifth_Periodic_Review_of_Westminster_constituencies" title="Fifth Periodic Review of Westminster constituencies">Fifth Periodic Review of Westminster constituencies</a>, Parliament increased the number of seats in the county from five to six for the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-BCECornwall_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BCECornwall-13">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> thus St Ives saw a loss of wards to the new <a href="/wiki/Camborne_and_Redruth_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Camborne and Redruth (UK Parliament constituency)">Camborne and Redruth seat</a>, including the St Ives Bay town of <a href="/wiki/Hayle" title="Hayle">Hayle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-offd_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-offd-14">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Civil_parishes_of_St_Ives_constituency" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3"><div><i><a href="/wiki/Portal:Cornwall" title="Portal:Cornwall">Cornwall Portal</a></i></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members_of_Parliament">Members of Parliament</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Members of Parliament">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="1558.E2.80.931629"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1558\xe2\x80\x931629">1558\xe2\x80\x931629</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1558\xe2\x80\x931629">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<td>Parliament of 1558\n</td>\n<td><a href="/w/index.php?title=St_Ives_(UK_Parliament_constituency)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">A <a href="/wiki/County_constituency" class="mw-redirect" title="County constituency">county constituency</a> (for the purposes of election expenses and type of returning officer)</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As with all constituencies, the constituency elects one <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">Member of Parliament</a> (MP) by the <a href="/wiki/First_past_the_post" class="mw-redirect" title="First past the post">first past the post</a> system of election at least every five years.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-4">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Earls of Buckinghamshire from 1746</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lord of a local <a href="/wiki/Manorialism" title="Manorialism">manor</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Presumably qualified voters, ensuring that it would be futile to contest here.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">in his <i>Representative History of Great Britain and Ireland</i></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Even though its MP from <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_1906" title="United Kingdom general election, 1906">1906</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sir_Clifford_Cory,_1st_Baronet" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Clifford Cory, 1st Baronet">Sir Clifford Cory</a>, was nominally a <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_(UK)" title="Liberal Party (UK)">Liberal</a> rather than a Unionist and stood against Liberal Unionists, he consistently stated his opposition to Irish Home Rule to voters at each election.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Possibly this is <a href="/wiki/John_Harington_(treasurer)" title="John Harington (treasurer)">John Harington (treasurer)</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Dictionary_of_National_Biography" title="Dictionary of National Biography">Dictionary of National Biography</a> records that Blount was elected for Berealston, which he certainly represented in the following two Parliaments; but Browne Willis (whose information on the Parliament of 1584-5 Neale refers to as "fairly reliable") gives two other names for Berealston and lists Blount for St Ives</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Lisle was also elected for <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth_(Isle_of_Wight)_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Yarmouth (Isle of Wight) (UK Parliament constituency)">Yarmouth (Isle of Wight)</a>, which he chose to represent, and did not sit for St Ives</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In April 1660, St Ives made a double return; on 5 May 1660, the Commons resolved "That John St Aubyn and James Praed, esqrs, being duly returned by the proper officers, they ought to sit".</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Hobart was also elected for <a href="/wiki/Norwich_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Norwich (UK Parliament constituency)">Norwich</a>, which he chose to represent, and never sat for St Ives</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-21">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On petition, Praed was declared not to have been duly elected, and a by-election was held</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-22">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Created The Lord Newborough (in the <a href="/wiki/Peerage_of_Ireland" title="Peerage of Ireland">Peerage of Ireland</a>) in 1776</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
